<script>
function sortTable(n) {
  var table, rows, switching, i, x, y, shouldSwitch, dir, switchcount = 0;
  table = document.getElementById("myTable");
  switching = true;
  //Set the sorting direction to ascending:
  dir = "asc"; 
  /*Make a loop that will continue until
  no switching has been done:*/
  while (switching) {
    //start by saying: no switching is done:
    switching = false;
    rows = table.rows;
    /*Loop through all table rows (except the
    first, which contains table headers):*/
    for (i = 1; i < (rows.length - 1); i++) {
      //start by saying there should be no switching:
      shouldSwitch = false;
      /*Get the two elements you want to compare,
      one from current row and one from the next:*/
      x = rows[i].getElementsByTagName("TD")[n];
      y = rows[i + 1].getElementsByTagName("TD")[n];
      /*check if the two rows should switch place,
      based on the direction, asc or desc:*/
      if (dir == "asc") {
        if (x.innerHTML.toLowerCase() > y.innerHTML.toLowerCase()) {
          //if so, mark as a switch and break the loop:
          shouldSwitch= true;
          break;
        }
      } else if (dir == "desc") {
        if (x.innerHTML.toLowerCase() < y.innerHTML.toLowerCase()) {
          //if so, mark as a switch and break the loop:
          shouldSwitch = true;
          break;
        }
      }
    }
    if (shouldSwitch) {
      /*If a switch has been marked, make the switch
      and mark that a switch has been done:*/
      rows[i].parentNode.insertBefore(rows[i + 1], rows[i]);
      switching = true;
      //Each time a switch is done, increase this count by 1:
      switchcount ++;      
    } else {
      /*If no switching has been done AND the direction is "asc",
      set the direction to "desc" and run the while loop again.*/
      if (switchcount == 0 && dir == "asc") {
        dir = "desc";
        switching = true;
      }
    }
  }
}
</script>

00.01 New Home: /newhome

<img alt="newho" data-align="center" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="90a53eae-d415-4e2d-a3f0-ba927d36d371" height="307" src="/sites/default/files/inline-images/PRECnewhome_0.png" width="1115" />

pagina:
title:
01.01 About Us: /about

content type:
Basic page	

Author:
pyralnet1_prec
 	
Source:
<p>About Us</p>

<p>The Project on Religion and Economic Change is made possible through the Spiritual Capital program of the Metanexus Institute and the Templeton Foundation. In 2005, Prof. Robert Woodberry was one of three scholars awarded multi-year grants to study the influence of “spiritual capital” on societies.</p>

<p>The Metanexus Institute is a respected educational center promoting the constructive engagement of science and religion. It seeks to create an enduring intellectual and social movement by collaborating with persons and communities from diverse religious traditions and scientific disciplines.</p>

<p>The John Templeton Foundation advances an appreciation for the critical importance of the moral and spiritual dimensions of life. By supporting studies which demonstrate the benefits of a progressive approach to learning in these areas, it is the Foundation's purpose to stimulate a fresh interchange between the theological and scientific communities. The Foundation currently funds more than 300 projects, studies, award programs and publications worldwide.</p>

<p>What is “Spiritual Capital?”</p>

<p>Religion is increasingly being recognized as an important factor in molding a diverse array of social phenomena. One of the chief ways it operates, social scientists believe, is through the building of networks and trust between individuals and groups, a concept referred to as “social capital.” Spiritual capital, then, may be thought of as a type of social capital, one that has a unique and specific origin in religious or spiritual beliefs and practices. The effects of this type of capital can be measured, evaluated, and compared as it is enacted by groups, such as missionary organizations or political parties, and individuals, such as the devout versus the nominally religious.</p>

<p>The application of spiritual capital in the context of the Project on Religion and Economic Change translates to an examination of the economic “return on spiritual investments” made by missionaries, religious leaders, and individuals around the world, within nations, communities, and in the lives of individuals. Thus, spiritual capital here takes on a precise and particularly appropriate meaning that will contribute substantively to our understanding of this important concept.</p>

title:
Articles, Publications, and Technical Reports

content type:
Basic page	

Author:
pyralnet1_prec
 	
Source:
<p>These are some examples of the scholarly productions related to our research:</p>

<ul>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry. 2012.<br />
	"The Missionary Roots of Liberal Democracy"&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/missionaryrootsofliberaldemocracy.pdf">( PDF )</a><br />
	American Political Science Review 106(2): 244-74<br />
	(Earned awards for the best article in <a href="http://community.apsanet.org/ComparativePolitics/awards/gregoryl">Comparative Politics</a>, <a href="http://www.apsanet.org/sections/sectionAwardDetail.cfm?section=Sec35">Comparative Democratization</a>, <a href="http://www.apsanet.org/sections/sectionAwardDetail.cfm?award=SEC25ABPW">Political Economy</a> (runner up) from the American Political Science Association and best article in the <a href="http://www.asanet.org/sections/religion_past_recipients">Sociology of Religion</a> from the American Sociological Association).&nbsp;</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry, Juan Carlos Esparza, Reid Porter, and Xiaoyun Lu. (version from July 2010)<br />
	Conceptual Framework and Technical Innovations for Creating the Project on Religion &amp; Economy Change Geo-Spatial Database (&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/Report20100922.pdf">PDF</a>&nbsp;)<br />
	(Our technical reports describe the process of our research including the main challenges we found and the strategies to face them.)</li>
	<li>Woodberry, Robert D. 2014.&nbsp;<br />
	“Looking Beyond the Usual Suspects: Integrating Religious Actors into the Study of Democratization and Economic Development.” <em>Comparative Democratization Newsletter, American Political Science Association</em> 12(1): 2, 16-19.&nbsp;</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry. 2013.<br />
	"Pentecostalism and Democracy: Is There a Relationship?"&nbsp;(&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/PentecotalismAndDemocracy_2007.pdf">PDF</a>&nbsp;)<br />
	pp. 119-137 <em>The Growth and Global Impact of Pentecostalism</em>.<br />
	Donald E. Miller, Kimon H. Sargeant and Richard Florey (eds.)<br />
	New York: Oxford University Press.</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry. 2008.<br />
	"Pentecostalism and Economic Development"&nbsp;&nbsp;(&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/Report20100922.pdf">PDF</a>&nbsp;)<br />
	p. 157-177 in Markets, Morals and Religion.<br />
	Jonathan B. Imber (ed.) New Brunswick, NJ: Transaction Publishers.</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry. 2007.<br />
	"The Social Impact of Missionary Higher Education"&nbsp;&nbsp;(&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/SocialImpact_2007.pdf">PDF</a>&nbsp;)<br />

	Philip Yuen Sang Leung and Peter Tze Ming Ng (eds.)<br />
	Hong Kong: Centre for the Study of Religion and Chinese Society.<br />
	Robert D. Woodberry. 2007.<br />

	pp. 123-127 in Encyclopedia of Missions and Missionaries.<br />
	Jonathan Bonk (ed.) New York: Routledge.</li>

	Jonathan Bonk (ed.) New York: Routledge.</li>

	Jonathan Bonk (ed.) New York: Routledge.</li>

	The Review of Faith and International Affairs. 4(1): 3-12.</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry. 2005.<br />

	Ph.D. dissertation, Sociology, University of North Carolina, Chapel Hill.</li>
	<li>Robert D. Woodberry and Timothy S. Shah. 2004.<br />
	"Christianity and Democracy: The Pioneering Protestants"&nbsp;&nbsp;(&nbsp;<a href="http://prec.com/PRECdocuments/ThePioneeringProtestants_2004.pdf">PDF</a>&nbsp;)<br />
	Journal of Democracy. 15(2): 47-61.<br />
	(Part of a series of articles on the relationship between different religious traditions and democracy. The article discusses the mixed, but generally positive roll Protestantism and missionary activity have played in the development of conditions that foster stable democratization.)</li>

	"Sociology of Religion"<br />
